Air Force, Air Force Materiel Command, Air Force Research Laboratory, Sensors Directorate&nbsp;requirement for research related to Precise Reference Sensing for Cognitive Electronic Warfare&nbsp;(PRESENCE).</p>\n\n<h4>BACKGROUND</h4>\n\n<p>Since the early 1990&rsquo;s, AFRL Sensors Directorate has been extremely successful in developing one-of-akind DoD radio frequency (RF) Navwar testbeds and constructive mission simulations. Innovative MSW&amp;A tools have been developed to characterize exploratory, advanced, and operational GPS systems in land, air, sea, and space environments. Past RDT&amp;E on-site awards in this area (the most recent being the Navigation Warfare Technology Research Modeling, Simulation, Wargaming &amp; Analysis (MSW&amp;A) (NWTRM) program) have attracted a variety of DoD and industry customers, as the testbeds provide a cost-effective means of effectively predicting and validating Navwar flight test results in a repeatable laboratory environment.</p>\n\n<h4>REQUIREMENTS</h4>\n\n<p>The objectives of this effort are to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>Perform Navigation Warfare (Navwar) technology research, including electronic attack (EA), electronic protection (EP), and electronic support (ES) techniques for cognitive electronic warfare (EW) applications across air, space, cyberspace, maritime, and land domains.</li>\n\t<li>Perform integrated Global Navigation Satellite System (GNSS) Position, Navigation &amp; Timing Assurance (PNTA), Modernized GPS User Equipment (MGUE) and Software Defined Radio (SDR) research.</li>\n\t<li>Develop and demonstrate algorithms and technology to optimize position, velocity, time, and frequency for airborne platforms at the sensor aperture for collaborative passive radar, Signal Intelligence (SIGINT), and EW techniques and systems. This includes absolute and relative position, velocity, time and frequency optimization in concert with military GPS receivers and associated EP technologies.</li>\n\t<li>Develop novel simulation technologies and/or enhance existing Navwar test assets for AFRL wargaming activities, Sensor Directorate System Integration Lab (SIL), and cross-Directorate research activities (e.g., RV Space Weather Ionospheric Scintillation and RW/RQ Hypersonic weapons).</li>\n\t<li>Develop a small size, weight, power, and cost (SWAP-C) Navwar testbed for lab, SIL, and flight test/training applications. This innovative testbed capability will enable real-time GNSS processing for Navwar EA, ES, and EP evaluations in live, virtual and constructive (LVC) test environments. The challenge will be to develop a ruggedized and reconfigurable testbed which is reduced at least 50% SWAP-C from the current Fieldable Antenna Wavefront Simulator (AWFS) Next Generation (FANG) Modular Design (FANG-MD). With respect to the software architecture, there will be extensive Graphical User Interface (GUI) development effort, creation of newly developed AWFS antenna models, generation of on-board jamming signals, trajectory generation capability, and standard input/output file structures. With respect to hardware development, the testbed will be much smaller than the current 2-man portable FANG-MD and will incorporate the latest Field Programmable Gate Array (FPGA) technology.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor will also conduct exploratory and advanced Navwar research using simulations and experiments in the Assured Position, Navigation and Timing (APNT) Concepts Exploration facility, and provide continued enhancement of the Navwar facility, which hosts the following capabilities (hereafter referred to as &ldquo;Navwar Testbed&rdquo;):&nbsp;\n\t<ul>\n\t\t<li>AWFS ?</li>\n\t\t<li>Virtual Flight Test (VFT)</li>\n\t\t<li>AWFS Next Generation (ANG)</li>\n\t\t<li>FANG</li>\n\t\t<li>ANG Inertial/GPS Synchronizer (AIGS)</li>\n\t\t<li>Joint Air-to-Surface Strike Missile (JASSM) ANG System Simulator (JASS)</li>\n\t\t<li>Time/Frequency of Arrival (T/FOA) ANG Modification Initiative (TAMI)</li>\n\t\t<li>GPS Interference and Navigation Tool (GIANT)</li>\n\t\t<li>Ionospheric Scintillation Interference System (ISIS)</li>\n\t\t<li>Rotor Blade Modulation (RBM)</li>\n\t\t<li>Hypersonic Navigation (HyNav)</li>\n\t\t<li>Vertical-sensing Effectiveness and CONOPS Tool for Operational Requirements (VECTOR)</li>\n\t\t<li>Multi-ship electronic support hardware-in-the-loop (MESH)</li>\n\t\t<li>FANG-MD</li>\n\t</ul>\n\t</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>Requirements:</p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>The contractor shall fabricate or acquire hardware, and write or acquire software and firmware as required to develop a reduced SWAP-C FANG-MD testbed capability usable across the air, space, cyberspace, maritime, and land domains for Navwar EA, ES, and EP applications.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall modify, enhance, and maintain the current Navwar Testbed capabilities in the ACE facility to ensure this testbed is capable of supporting layered sensing missions.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall perform analyses with the Navwar Testbed on emerging technologies and conduct laboratory demonstrations using systems or simulations which utilize the technologies of interest.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall conduct technology and feasibility studies with the Navwar Testbed of exploratory and advanced technologies as a basis for Navwar research.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall develop GNSS anti-jam antenna simulation technologies as well as the design and development of prototype hardware for risk reduction and proof-of concept. Such designs shall be compatible and interoperable with the Navwar Testbed.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall conduct mission capability and performance analyses for Navwar Testbed applications.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall facilitate associate agreements, as required, with original equipment manufacturers, subcontractors, or other specialists that are critical to satisfying requirements for the innovative Navwar Testbed, including equipment maintenance. The contractor shall enter into nondisclosure agreements, as required, to complete tasks under this SOO.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall provide materials, replacement components, and parts in a timely manner in efforts to prevent or eliminate malfunctions, enhance or upgrade capabilities, or improve performance capabilities in the ACE facility. The contractor shall make hardware and software procurements and developments, as required, for ACE facility maintenance and enhancements.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall design, develop, integrate, and test software in the ACE facility. As part of this SOO, the contractor will perform backup of computer system data, patch and upgrade commercial software packages, and maintain computer security certification and accreditation packages.</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall perform end-of-day security checks in the ACE facility on an as needed basis. When required to perform end-of-day security checks in the ACE facility, the contractor shall follow the procedures defined in AFRL Memo for Record dated 8 April 2008 titled &quot;Contractor Procedures for Closing the Advanced Concepts Exploration (ACE) Lab at the End of Day (EOD).&quot;</li>\n\t<li>The contractor shall plan, execute, and manage tasks required to configure the ACE facility and Navwar Testbed for comprehensive evaluation of a wide variety of anti-jam systems, including, but not limited to:\n\t<ul>\n\t\t<li>Small Antenna System (SAS)</li>\n\t\t<li>Joint Precision Approach and Landing System (JPALS)</li>\n\t\t<li>Integrated GPS Antenna System (GAS)</li>\n\t\t<li>Reaper</li>\n\t\t<li>Predator</li>\n\t\t<li>Small Diameter Bomb (SDB)</li>\n\t\t<li>Massive Ordinance Penetrator (MOP)</li>\n\t\t<li>F-15</li>\n\t\t<li>F-16</li>\n\t\t<li>A-10</li>\n\t\t<li>B-2</li>\n\t\t<li>JASSM</li>\n\t</ul>\n\t</li>\n\t<li>As part of this task, the contractor shall, as required, purchase, development, and construct additional hardware, firmware, or software required for successful completion of the task.
